href=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/21/nutrimost-ultimate-fat-loss-system-slammed-with-32-million-judgment-for-overblown-weight-loss-claims/\" title=\"NutriMost ‘Ultimate Fat Loss’ System Slammed With $32 Million Judgment For Overblown Weight Loss&nbsp;Claims\" rel=\"bookmark\">NutriMost ‘Ultimate Fat Loss’ System Slammed With $32 Million Judgment For Overblown Weight Loss&nbsp;Claims</a></h2> \n<div class=\"post-info\">By <span class=\"author vcard\"><span class=\"fn\"><a href=\"https://consumerist.com/author/chrismorranconsumerist/\" title=\"Posts by Chris Morran\" class=\"author url fn\" rel=\"author\">Chris Morran</a></span></span>  <span class=\"date published time\" title=\"2017-04-21T17:06:28+00:00\">April 21, 2017</span> </div><div class=\"entry-content\"><div class=\"has-content-area\" data-url=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/21/nutrimost-ultimate-fat-loss-system-slammed-with-32-million-judgment-for-overblown-weight-loss-claims/\" data-title=\"NutriMost ‘Ultimate Fat Loss’ System Slammed With $32 Million Judgment For Overblown Weight Loss&nbsp;Claims\"><p>The marketing for the NutriMost Ultimate Fat Loss system claimed that users could drop 40 pounds, or more, in just 40 days, and without having to fret about calories. However, the Federal Trade Commission says that this $1,900 program is not backed by <i>any</i> science, actually requires a starvation-level diet, uses before-and-after examples from people related to the company, and forces customers to sign agreements that prevent them from saying anything bad about the program. <a href=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/21/nutrimost-ultimate-fat-loss-system-slammed-with-32-million-judgment-for-overblown-weight-loss-claims/#more-10275827\" class=\"more-link\">[More]</a></p>\n</div><div id=\"jp-post-flair\" class=\"sharedaddy sd-like-enabled sd-sharing-enabled\"><div class=\"sharedaddy sd-sharing-enabled\"><div class=\"robots-nocontent Loan&nbsp;Operations</a></h2> \n<div class=\"post-info\">By <span class=\"author vcard\"><span class=\"fn\"><a href=\"https://consumerist.com/author/ashleekielerconsumerist/\" title=\"Posts by Ashlee Kieler\" class=\"author url fn\" rel=\"author\">Ashlee Kieler</a></span></span>  <span class=\"date published time\" title=\"2017-04-21T16:24:26+00:00\">April 21, 2017</span> </div><div class=\"entry-content\"><div class=\"has-content-area\" data-url=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/21/financial-choice-act-2-0-would-eliminate-governments-ability-to-go-after-shady-payday-loan-operations/\" data-title=\"‘Financial Choice Act 2.0’ Would Eliminate Government’s Ability To Go After Shady Payday Loan&nbsp;Operations\"><p>Even though recent surveys indicate that the overwhelming <a href=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/19/most-americans-favor-payday-loan-reforms/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">majority of Americans want <i>more</i> regulation of payday class=\"Thumbnail thumbnail large alignleft post-image\"></a><h2 class=\"entry-title\"><a href=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/21/twitch-wants-to-let-more-people-make-some-money-from-livestreaming-video-games/\" title=\"Twitch Wants To Let More People Make Some Money From Livestreaming Video&nbsp;Games\" rel=\"bookmark\">Twitch Wants To Let More People Make Some Money From Livestreaming Video&nbsp;Games</a></h2> \n<div class=\"post-info\">By <span class=\"author vcard\"><span class=\"fn\"><a href=\"https://consumerist.com/author/kcoxconsumer/\" title=\"Posts by Kate Cox\" class=\"author url fn\" rel=\"author\">Kate Cox</a></span></span>  <span class=\"date published time\" title=\"2017-04-21T15:59:12+00:00\">April 21, 2017</span> </div><div class=\"entry-content\"><div class=\"has-content-area\" data-url=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/21/twitch-wants-to-let-more-people-make-some-money-from-livestreaming-video-games/\" data-title=\"Twitch Wants To Let More People Make Some Money From Livestreaming Video&nbsp;Games\"><p>Video, video, video. That’s basically all any and every platform wants to talk about, here in 2017: how much video it can stream, and how many people are watching it. But one step in getting people to watch live video on your platform is making sure the folks making those videos have an incentive to <i>keep</i> making them. There’s only so much people will do for their own amusement. So what better enticement than more money? <a href=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/21/twitch-wants-to-let-more-people-make-some-money-from-livestreaming-video-games/#more-10275831\" class=\"Thumbnail thumbnail large alignleft post-image\"></a><h2 class=\"entry-title\"><a href=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/21/plastc-smart-cards-raise-9m-in-pre-orders-wont-ever-ship/\" title=\"Plastc Smart Cards Raise $9M In Pre-Orders, Won’t Ever&nbsp;Ship\" rel=\"bookmark\">Plastc Smart Cards Raise $9M In Pre-Orders, Won’t Ever&nbsp;Ship</a></h2> \n<div class=\"post-info\">By <span class=\"author vcard\"><span class=\"fn\"><a href=\"https://consumerist.com/author/consumerlaura/\" title=\"Posts by Laura Northrup\" class=\"author url fn\" rel=\"author\">Laura Northrup</a></span></span>  <span class=\"date published time\" title=\"2017-04-21T15:30:48+00:00\">April 21, 2017</span> </div><div class=\"entry-content\"><div class=\"has-content-area\" data-url=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/21/plastc-smart-cards-raise-9m-in-pre-orders-wont-ever-ship/\" data-title=\"Plastc Smart Cards Raise $9M In Pre-Orders, Won’t Ever&nbsp;Ship\"><p>A few years ago, universal payment cards were a mini-fad online. The idea was that you carried one “smart” card which stored the numbers of all of your other credit cards. The most popular was Coin, which was ultimately acquired by Fitbit <a href=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/02/01/fitbit-kills-off-its-coin-payment-service-devices-to-become-useless-when-batteries-die/\" target=\"_blank\">and shut down</a>. Another card was Plastc, which has brought in $9 million through pre-orders since 2014, but has yet to ship — and is now out of business  <a href=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/21/plastc-smart-cards-raise-9m-in-pre-orders-wont-ever-ship/#more-10275830\" class=\"more-link\">[More]</a></p>\n</div><div id=\"jp-post-flair\" Account Settlement; Will Cover Customers Going Back To&nbsp;2002\" rel=\"bookmark\">Wells Fargo Adds Another $32 Million To Fake Account Settlement; Will Cover Customers Going Back To&nbsp;2002</a></h2> \n<div class=\"post-info\">By <span class=\"author vcard\"><span class=\"fn\"><a href=\"https://consumerist.com/author/chrismorranconsumerist/\" title=\"Posts by Chris Morran\" class=\"author url fn\" rel=\"author\">Chris Morran</a></span></span>  <span class=\"date published time\" title=\"2017-04-21T10:19:35+00:00\">April 21, 2017</span> </div><div class=\"entry-content\"><div class=\"has-content-area\" data-url=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/21/wells-fargo-adds-another-32-million-to-fake-account-settlement-will-cover-customers-going-back-to-2002/\" data-title=\"Wells Fargo Adds Another $32 Million To Fake Account Settlement; Will Cover Customers Going Back To&nbsp;2002\"><p>Wells Fargo recently <a href=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/03/29/wells-fargo-says-it-will-pay-110-million-to-settle-fake-account-fiasco-class-action/\" target=\"_blank\">reached a $110 million deal</a> that it hoped would close the books on a variety of class action lawsuits related to <a href=\"https://consumerist.com/tag/fake-account-fiasco/\" target=\"_blank\">millions of fake accounts</a> opened by Wells employees trying to game the bank’s system of sales quotas and incentives. That settlement was intended to cover affected Wells customers going back through 2009, but it’s now been expanded by $32 million to add compensation for bank accounts as far back as 2002. <a href=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/21/wells-fargo-adds-another-32-million-to-fake-account-settlement-will-cover-customers-going-back-to-2002/#more-10275777\" ‘Beauty Influencers’\" rel=\"bookmark\">Suave Pours Some Shampoo In A Different Bottle, Tries To Trick ‘Beauty Influencers’</a></h2> \n<div class=\"post-info\">By <span class=\"author vcard\"><span class=\"fn\"><a href=\"https://consumerist.com/author/consumerlaura/\" title=\"Posts by Laura Northrup\" class=\"author url fn\" rel=\"author\">Laura Northrup</a></span></span>  <span class=\"date published time\" title=\"2017-04-20T17:15:42+00:00\">April 20, 2017</span> </div><div class=\"entry-content\"><div class=\"has-content-area\" data-url=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/20/suave-pours-some-shampoo-in-a-different-bottle-tries-to-trick-beauty-influencers/\" data-title=\"Suave Pours Some Shampoo In A Different Bottle, Tries To Trick ‘Beauty Influencers’\"><p>Unilever has apparently noticed that <a href=\"https://consumerist.com/2016/05/26/its-not-about-whats-in-beauty-products-these-days-its-about-what-isnt/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">some young women are more concerned about what ingredients <em>aren’t</em> in their beauty products</a> and sneer at the items sold in drug stores and big-box stores. It has responded with a campaign where it tricks a diverse cast of online “beauty influencers” into trying a new product with sleek packaging for two weeks. That product? Rebottled Suave. <a href=\"https://consumerist.com/2017/04/20/suave-pours-some-shampoo-in-a-different-bottle-tries-to-trick-beauty-influencers/#more-10275748\"
